I can't recall who the seller was, so this review is not made against this retailer (I know it was not directly sold by Amazon, but by a third party). In general I wanted to make sure that customers were aware of this:<br /><br />Amazon is not an authorized retailer of Clarisonic. That means that Clarisonic will not offer any warranty service for a Clarisonic you purchase through Amazon.<br /><br />About a month after receiving the Clarisonic Mia, I started noticing that the prongs holding the brush were starting to rust. Considering the manual says you can take the unit in the shower, it seemed odd that the prongs would be rusting. I contacted Clarisonic to see if they had other complaints. They asked me for an ID number located on the bottom of the handle, which my unit had. She told me that that ID was not valid and asked where I purchased it. That's when I found out that they would not honor any warranties against units purchased on Amazon and that likely what I received was a counterfeit unit.<br /><br />I then contacted Amazon and although it was past the standard 30 day return time frame, they offered to take back the unit and credit my husband's credit card. They did charge me a restocking fee, which is odd, because I really hope they did not restock that counterfeit unit.<br /><br />I still LOVE Amazon and have purchased many things since this incident about 6 months ago. Their customer service was prompt and nice when I made the return, and although I did not receive 100% of the refund, the 80% I did receive was better than nothing. Just be forewarned that if you need to make a warranty claim, Clarisonic may not accept it.

  187. I was given a Mia for Christmas last year, as a gift from my sister. Never once did I think it was a fake. I had no idea this was even an issue, until I recently stumbled upon a you tuber, who had said there was a problem with knock-offs. All of the tell tale signs that mine was a knock-off, I had. The biggest being that the pins that hold my brushes in place, rusted (and they rusted within the first month, I never really thought to look into it, because I really only use it once or twice a week). I do however, because of the rust issue, remove my brush every time I use it, to wash it and also to prevent further rusting.<br /><br />There ARE resellers on Amazon, that could very well be authorized to sell Clarisonic, but seeing the seller being listed as &#34;Clarisonic,&#34; is not true.<br /><br />There are tell tale signs that you could have a knock-off:<br /><br />- The brush is hard to remove or put in.<br />- There should be even spacing between all of the letters on the logo. If you have an uneven space between the Cl and the a in &#34;Clairsonic&#34; (Cl arisonic), it's a knock-off.<br />- If you have a space in between your serial number, it's probably a knock-off.<br />- If your pins rust, you get the idea. The pins are the biggest red-flag. They shouldn't rust.<br /><br />The best way to tell, is to call Clarisonic to register your product. They will let you know, when you register the serial number. This was my biggest mistake. But my busy life doesn't lend to me remembering to do these sorts of things. Better yet, the best way to assure you're getting an authentic product, is to either purchase directly from their website, OR, an authorized seller, which are all listed on Clarisonic's website.

It shuts off after one minute, but I usually go for two - I usually use it morning and night, weighing in at 4-5 minutes a day. Basically, depending on how much I'm using it, I end up having to charge it every 3ish days and the magnetic pLink charger is not as convenient as plopping it in the cradle charger. BUT, this is really a small compromise for saving some major dough and I don't mind that much...except when I forget to put it on the charger. :) (It does have a varying number of beeps go off when you first start the brush to let you know how much battery you have...so, I shouldn't complain!)<br /><br />Word of caution - Don't get carried away. :) I've always heard this and thought &#34;yeah, yeah, that won't happen to me&#34; but you can accidentally over-exfoliate. It feels so good, sometimes I just wanna push the little button again and let my face stay on the magic carpet ride a little longer. Delayed ouch. It took a few days for my raw, red cheeks to fully recover. Now, sometimes I'll only do it at night or skip a couple days...I try to pay attention to my skin's mood a little more and not get distracted by the foamy massage-y goodness. :)<br /><br />Btw, I alternate between the sensitive brush head and the acne-prone brush head. Happy brushing!

SOME TIPS: Instructions provided with the Clarisonic are so streamlined; I think they leave out some helpful hints. FYI, here are the steps my daughter and I take to cleanse with Clarisonic: 1. Use fingers to gently apply cleansing solution all around face.. 2. Turn on machine and cleanse as per Clarisonic instructions, starting with forehead, then nose/chin, and finally cheeks. (It may tickle the nose area the first few times, but tickling goes away with time...) 3. Rinse face well by splashing with warm water. 4. Pat dry face, then apply a light facial moisturizer. 5. Rinse Clarisonic brush and leave to air dry.
